2b. ENDOTYPE NAME: "The Slow Burn"

The Slow Burn captures the core mechanism driving Moj Mahdara's clinical picture: a genetically throttled metabolism in which every major clearing and processing pathway is constitutionally slowed â€” COMT (catecholamines), GSTM1 (detoxification, entirely absent), MTHFR (methylation, 44% activity), DIO2 (thyroid conversion), NAT2 (acetylation) â€” while chronic low-grade inflammation slowly consumes reserves faster than her impaired biochemistry can replenish them.

This is not a sudden collapse. It is a progressive erosion of metabolic reserves that has been unfolding over years. The fire doesn't rage; it smolders. Each year, ferritin rises a little more (inflammatory sequestration), DHEA-S drops a little further (adrenal depletion), fibrinogen climbs (hepatic inflammatory drive), and the IR Score worsens despite aggressive pharmaceutical intervention. The perimenopause transition â€” beginning around 2024 â€” added fuel to this slow burn by withdrawing the protective effects of estrogen on metabolism, cardiovascular function, and cognition.

The paradox at the center of this case: how can so many things be getting worse when so many things are being treated? The answer is that the treatments are targeting downstream symptoms without addressing the upstream genetic bottlenecks that create the backlog in the first place.

2c. UNIFYING NARRATIVE

Moj Mahdara's clinical picture emerges from a genetic architecture that systematically limits the speed and efficiency of her core metabolic pathways. She carries a COMT AA (Met/Met) slow metabolizer genotype that prolongs dopamine, norepinephrine, and catechol estrogen exposure; a GSTM1 null deletion that completely eliminates Phase II glutathione conjugation; a compound MTHFR heterozygote (C677T/A1298C) that reduces methylation cycle throughput to 44% of normal; a DIO2 CC variant that impairs tissue-level conversion of T4 to the active thyroid hormone T3; dual insulin resistance variants (PPARG CC + IRS1 CC) that blunt insulin signaling; and a MAOA TT variant that compounds the neurotransmitter processing burden created by slow COMT. Each of these variants alone would be manageable. Together, they create a metabolic system that is constitutionally running at reduced capacity â€” a bottleneck at every junction.

This genetic substrate remained largely compensated until 2019, when two diagnoses arrived simultaneously: hypothyroidism and PCOS. Something â€” chronic stress (COMT AA makes her exquisitely stress-sensitive), autoimmune activation (thyroglobulin antibodies were elevated by 2022 at 15.9 IU/mL), or the long-running vitamin D deficiency (diagnosed since 2009, never adequately corrected) â€” tipped the system past its ability to compensate. The DIO2 CC genotype meant that even with Armour Thyroid (which contains both T4 and T3), her tissues were not fully receiving the thyroid signal. The PPARG CC + IRS1 CC genotype meant that insulin resistance was not just a lifestyle disease but a genetic predisposition, one that metabolic interventions could only partially overcome. By the time of the bilateral mastectomy in 2021 and the onset of perimenopause by 2024, her system was already in deficit â€” and the withdrawal of endogenous estrogen (further impaired by CYP19A1 TT aromatase variant) accelerated every downstream cascade: cardiovascular risk, inflammation, bone density, cognitive function, and gut integrity.

Why do seemingly unrelated findings connect? Because the "slow" genetic architecture means every system competes for the same limited metabolic resources. When methylation is impaired (MTHFR 44%), there is less SAM for COMT to methylate catecholamines, less substrate for PEMT to make phosphatidylcholine for bile and cell membranes, and less cysteine flux through the transsulfuration pathway for glutathione synthesis â€” which is already catastrophically limited by GSTM1 null. When thyroid conversion is impaired (DIO2 CC), basal metabolic rate drops, the gut slows, inflammation clearance slows, and the brain's executive function declines. When insulin resistance is genetic (PPARG + IRS1), Mounjaro can produce excellent weight loss (30+ lbs) and normalize glucose metrics (HbA1c 4.9%, fasting glucose 68), yet the IR Score paradoxically worsens (42â†’48) because the genetic component of insulin signaling dysfunction persists independent of adiposity. Every module feeds every other module, and the whole system burns slowly.

2d. MODULE BREAKDOWN
↑ Back to top
MODULE 1: THE GENETIC SLOW ARCHITECTURE

"The Bottleneck Blueprint" (Lifelong)

This module establishes the genetic foundation: every major metabolic clearing pathway in this patient is constitutionally throttled. This is the soil in which all disease grows.

Clinical Implication for Module 1: The genetic architecture cannot be changed. All interventions must work WITH these bottlenecks by providing downstream products directly (methylfolate, methylcobalamin, glutathione/NAC, T3-containing thyroid hormone) rather than relying on endogenous conversion through impaired pathways.

MODULE 2: THE THYROID-METABOLIC TRAP

"Burning Without Fuel" (2019 â†’ Present)

This module explains how DIO2 CC + hypothyroidism + PPARG/IRS1 insulin resistance genetics create a self-reinforcing trap where metabolic function declines even as treatments target individual symptoms.

Clinical Implication for Module 2: The thyroid medication question must be resolved IMMEDIATELY. If not on Armour, reinitiate with T3-containing preparation (not levothyroxine alone due to DIO2 CC). MODULE 3: THE GUT-IMMUNE BREACH

"The Unguarded Gate" (2018 â†’ Present)

This module explains how GSTM1 null + HNMT AA + DAO CG + CYP2R1 GG + vitamin D insufficiency create a gut-immune vulnerability that manifests as maximum dysbiosis, parasitic infection, and histamine intolerance.

**Clinical Implication for Module 3:** Before retreating dysbiosis, fix the environment: (1) Vitamin D to >50 ng/mL via high-dose D3 or calcifediol, (2) Glutathione/NAC support for GSTM1 null, (3) Thyroid optimization for gut motility. Only then will antimicrobial/probiotic interventions have a hospitable environment to restore. Treat Dientamoeba fragilis with targeted antiparasitic.

**Clinical Implication for Module 6:** Brain fog will NOT resolve from a single intervention. It requires: (1) Thyroid optimization (DIO2 CC â†’ T3-containing therapy), (2) Histamine management (dust mite reduction, DAO enzyme, HNMT support with SAMe/magnesium), (3) Inflammation reduction (address gut dysbiosis, full-dose Metformin), (4) Serotonin support (5-HTP or tryptophan, with caution given MAOA TT), (5) Continued methylation support (MB12, methylfolate). Strattera switch was appropriate for COMT AA.

PARADOX RESOLUTION INDEX

# Paradox Resolution Module
1 IR Score worsening despite weight loss + Mounjaro Genetic IR floor (PPARG + IRS1) + lipid-weighted scoring + Metformin underdosing 2
2 Rising Ferritin with low MCHC Inflammatory iron sequestration (IL-6 GG â†’ hepcidin), not overload 4
3 FSH suppressed despite menopausal AMH Iatrogenic suppression from exogenous estrogen + progesterone overcompliance 5
4 Normal thyroid labs but missing medication DIO2 CC means serum is misleading for tissue status; requires patient clarification 2
5 Maximum dysbiosis despite antimicrobial protocols CYP2R1 GG â†’ vitamin D stuck â†’ LL-37 underpowered; GSTM1 null â†’ hostile gut environment 3
6 Chronic vitamin D insufficiency despite supplementation CYP2R1 GG impairs hepatic 25-hydroxylation; needs higher dose or calcifediol 3
7 MPO improved while fibrinogen rises Different pathways: MPO = vascular (resolved), fibrinogen = hepatic (IL-6 GG + IR drive) 4
8 OMICm Age 42 vs Symphony Age 53.1 OMICm reflects Mounjaro metabolic improvement; Symphony (53.1) is more reliable biological age 6

PART 3: RECOMMENDATIONS

Genetically-Informed, Prioritized Intervention Plan

Patient: Moj Mahdara Report Generated: 2026-02-11 Endotype: "The Slow Burn" â€” Multi-System Metabolic Bottleneck Pipeline Run: 20260210_Moj

3a. CURRENT PROTOCOL ASSESSMENT

Assessment Date: 2026-02-11 Framework: Each item classified by endotype relevance

CLASSIFICATION KEY
✅ KEEP — Directly targets endotype mechanism; correctly formulated 🟢 OK — Supportive/general benefit; may continue 🔧 MODIFY — Right target, wrong form/dose/schedule ⏸️ PAUSE — Temporarily discontinue during restructuring ❌ DISCONTINUE — Wrong form or counterproductive 🚨 CRITICAL — Requires immediate action or clarification

🚨 CRITICAL — Requires Immediate Action

🚨 Armour Thyroid (STATUS UNKNOWN) CRITICAL
If currently taking: KEEP. DIO2 CC requires T3-containing thyroid medication. If stopped: REINSTATE IMMEDIATELY. Levothyroxine-only would be inadequate for this genotype. See Protocol #1.
🚨 Estrace vaginal cream (NEVER TAKEN) CRITICAL
Prescribed but NEVER TAKEN. Severe urethral atrophy documented by Dr. Kim. Local estrogen is LOW systemic risk. Must address compliance barrier. See Protocol #5, Section 5.4.
🚨 Cyanocobalamin 1000mcg IM monthly DISCONTINUE
WRONG FORM. Cyanocobalamin requires MTHFR-dependent conversion. With MTHFR compound het (44% activity), cyanocobalamin is poorly converted. Dr. West recommended MB12 injections 3x/week — ⚠ COMPLIANCE UNCONFIRMED. If patient is only getting cyano: SWITCH to methylcobalamin or hydroxocobalamin immediately.

🔧 MODIFY — Right Target, Wrong Form/Dose/Schedule

🔧 Vitamin D Sun (30) — 1-2 caps MODIFY
Correct target but WRONG DOSE for CYP2R1 GG genotype. Current dose insufficient (level stuck at 34-35 for 3+ years). Increase to 5000-10000 IU/day OR switch to calcifediol. See Protocol #2 for details.
🔧 Magnesium Citrate 1000mg HS MODIFY
Magnesium is a COMT cofactor — essential for COMT AA patient. However, citrate form is primarily laxative at this dose. Split: Mag glycinate 400mg (COMT support, daytime) + Mag threonate 200mg (brain, evening) + Mag citrate 400mg (bowel, bedtime). See Protocol #3.
🔧 LL-37 100mcg SC daily MODIFY
Antimicrobial peptide addressing dysbiosis 10/10. HOWEVER: LL-37 requires vitamin D >50 ng/mL for optimal expression. At current D level (35), LL-37 is underpowered. MODIFICATION: Raise vitamin D to >50 ng/mL FIRST, then resume LL-37 cycling. Bilateral mastectomy noted — maintain caution per precautions at proper dosing.
🔧 Progesterone 100mg SR nightly MODIFY
Progesterone is needed for endometrial protection (even post-menopause) and sleep/mood (GABAergic metabolite allopregnanolone). MODIFICATION: Switch from continuous (patient takes nightly) to CYCLIC dosing: days 10-24 of calendar month ONLY. Continuous use is suppressing FSH (12.6 at age 49 with AMH <0.08 = iatrogenic suppression) and masking true menopausal status. See Protocol #5.
🔧 Lamotrigine 100mg/day (taking 50mg) MODIFY
Mood stabilizer — but MUST increase to prescribed 100mg (currently only 50mg). Lamotrigine does not burden COMT or NAT2 pathways. Underdosing may contribute to mood instability.
🔧 Metformin 1000mg/day (taking 500mg) MODIFY
Critical for PPARG CC + IRS1 CC genetic IR. MUST increase to prescribed 1000mg BID. Half-dosing undermines IR management. Consider extended-release if GI tolerance is the barrier.

✅ KEEP — Core Protocol, Genetically Supported

✅ Mounjaro (tirzepatide) 15mg/wk KEEP
Excellent response (30+ lbs). Addresses PPARG CC + IRS1 CC genetic IR via GLP-1/GIP dual agonism. Continue at current dose.
✅ Atomoxetine (Strattera) 40mg KEEP
Correct switch from Adderall for COMT AA. Strattera is a NRI that bypasses COMT-dependent catecholamine release. No dopamine surge = no palpitations. Genetically optimal ADHD medication.
✅ MB12 injections 3x/week (Dr. West Rx) KEEP — IF TAKING
⚠ COMPLIANCE UNCONFIRMED. Dr. West recommended MB12 (methylcobalamin) 3x/week. Patient self-report lists only CYANOCOBALAMIN 1000mcg IM monthly (Dr. Kurtz). Cyanocobalamin is the WRONG form for MTHFR compound het (44%). If only cyanocobalamin: SWITCH to methylcobalamin or hydroxocobalamin. Step 5 pipeline model (85%) is overstated — MTR AA=normal; burden from MTRR AG (low) + TCN2 CG (medium).
✅ MIC injections 3x/week KEEP
Methionine/Inositol/Choline — supports methylation cycle. Choline compensates for PEMT impairment (COMT AA uses SAM that PEMT also needs). Supports bile flow and hepatic detox.
✅ Nattokinase 1 cap/day KEEP
Fibrinolytic — addresses F2 GA + fibrinogen 427. Part of triple anticoagulant protocol. Continue monitoring with D-dimer.
✅ Lumbrokinase 3 caps/day KEEP
Potent fibrinolytic — complements nattokinase. Essential with rising fibrinogen (427) and F2 GA prothrombin variant.
✅ Baby Aspirin 81mg KEEP
Antiplatelet — non-overlapping mechanism with fibrinolytics. F2 GA warrants antiplatelet + fibrinolytic combination. Double when flying is appropriate for thrombotic risk.
✅ DAO Enzyme — before meals KEEP
Directly addresses DAO CG (rs1049793) enzyme deficiency. Replaces missing extracellular histamine clearance capacity.
⚡ ACTION: Increase to before EVERY meal — not just once daily. DAO CG = reduced enzyme.
✅ Hist (Quercetin) BID KEEP
Mast cell stabilizer — reduces histamine release upstream. Addresses chronic IgE elevation (312 IU/mL, 3.6x ULN). Synergizes with DAO enzyme for dual histamine management.
✅ Omega-3 Fish Oil 2 caps KEEP
Anti-inflammatory — addresses IL-6 GG pro-inflammatory genotype. FADS1 GT + FADS2 CG = reduced endogenous omega-3 conversion. Preformed EPA/DHA bypasses this. Continue.
✅ Inflamafree (Turmeric) BID KEEP
Curcumin — potent NF-kB inhibitor. Addresses IL-6 GG + CRP 2.1. Part of the anti-inflammatory stack that resolved MPO.
✅ Cholesterol Complete BID KEEP
Targets ApoB-driven lipid profile (LDL-P 1649, Pattern B→A). LDL-P improving. Continue until cardiovascular reassessment.
✅ DHEA 5mg AM KEEP
DHEA-S declined 66% (217→73). Adrenal precursor support. Dose is conservative (5mg); may increase to 10-25mg based on repeat DHEA-S levels. Monitor testosterone levels.
✅ Pregnenolone 100mg AM KEEP
Excellent recovery: 2.98 → 25.0 (739%). Mother hormone supporting downstream cortisol, DHEA, and sex hormones. Continue current dose — it is working.
✅ Phosphatidylcholine AM KEEP
Provides choline substrate directly — compensates for PEMT impairment (SAM diverted to COMT). Supports bile, membranes, brain function. Genetically indicated.
✅ Digestive Enzymes 2 caps TID KEEP
Supports nutrient absorption in setting of gut dysbiosis 10/10. Continue through gut restoration protocol.
✅ Estradiol patch 0.05mg 2x/week KEEP
Transdermal estrogen — appropriate for perimenopause with CYP19A1 TT (reduced endogenous production). Transdermal avoids first-pass hepatic metabolism — better for clotting risk (F2 GA).
✅ Testosterone cream 0.2ml daily KEEP
Supports libido, cognition, muscle mass. SHBG CC + CC (both no_impact) = normal binding. Continue and monitor levels.

🟢 OK — Supportive, May Continue

🟢 Alprazolam 0.5mg PRN OK
Long-standing PRN use (since 2009). Well-controlled anxiety. Monitor: benzodiazepine + GABA stack (Gabatrol) = additive CNS depression risk. Consider gradual taper as other interventions address root causes (histamine, thyroid, inflammation).
🟢 Pantoprazole 40mg (GLP-1 days) OK
Treats Mounjaro-induced GERD. Monitor: PPI long-term can impair B12 absorption (relevant with MTHFR/methylation burden), Mg absorption, and iron absorption (worsens inflammatory iron pattern). Use only on dosing days as prescribed.
🟢 Black Cumin Seed Oil OK
Thymoquinone — anti-inflammatory, some histamine benefit. Supportive but not primary mechanism-targeted. May continue.
🟢 Piracetam AM OK
Racetam nootropic — cognitive support. Reasonable given brain burden 49.3% and brain age +5.2yr. Not genetically specific. May continue if patient perceives benefit.
🟢 Brilliant Brain AM OK
Nootropic blend — overlaps with Piracetam and Phosphatidylcholine. Consider consolidating cognitive stack to reduce pill burden.
🟢 Vitamin C 1500mg OK
Antioxidant support. GSTO2 AG (rs156697) = medium risk for vitamin C recycling. 1500mg is adequate. Continue.
🟢 Electrolytes (Mg/K/Na blend) OK
Supportive — hydration and mineral balance. Continue.
🟢 Ultimate Recovery (Fish Oil/PREMS) OK
Overlaps with Omega-3. Consider consolidating to reduce pill burden. One high-quality omega-3 product sufficient.
🟢 Cyclease Menopause OK
Homeopathic menopause support. Low risk. May continue if patient perceives benefit. Not genetically targeted.
🟢 Melatonin 5mg nightly OK
Sleep support. 5mg is on the higher end — consider reducing to 0.5-1mg (physiologic dose). High-dose melatonin can suppress endogenous production and interact with hormone balance.
⏰ TIMING MATTERS: Take at or around sundown (7-8pm), NOT right before bed. Melatonin should mirror the natural circadian signal. Taking it at midnight or 2am defeats the purpose of circadian entrainment.
🟢 Gabatrol 2 caps (30 min pre-bed) OK
GABA-based sleep support. Caution: additive with Alprazolam (both GABAergic). Monitor for excessive sedation. Consider if needed long-term as anxiety root causes addressed.
🟢 CJC 1295 + Ipamorelin OK
GH secretagogue — supports body composition. Not genetically targeted but synergistic with Mounjaro for body recomposition. Monitor IGF-1 levels. Continue if clinician-supervised.
🟢 NAD+ 1000mg SC 3x/week OK
Supports mitochondrial function. PPARGC1A GG = reduced mito biogenesis, so NAD+ supplementation is theoretically supportive. Continue if tolerated.

🔧 ADD NEW — New Recommendation

🟣 L-Tryptophan 1000mg bedtime ADD NEW
Serotonin 48 (LOW, ref 56-244). Precursor to serotonin AND melatonin. Take with small carb snack. Start 500mg, titrate to 1g. HTR1A GG = reduced receptor sensitivity. Do NOT combine with 5-HTP — choose one pathway.

⏸️ PAUSE — Temporarily Discontinue

⏸️ TBC Probiotic 2 caps nightly PAUSE
Current probiotic is fighting a losing battle in a hostile gut environment (GSTM1 null, low vitamin D, D. fragilis present). PAUSE until gut environment is fixed (Protocol #2), then restart with targeted strains (Roseburia, Bifidobacterium, butyrate-producers matching deficit profile).

⚠ Compliance Unconfirmed — Biest/Estriol

⚠ Biest cream nightly (Dr. West Rx) KEEP — IF TAKING
Bi-est (estriol + estradiol) — topical. ⚠ COMPLIANCE UNCONFIRMED — not in patient self-report. If taking: monitor total estrogen exposure with DUTCH test (catechol estrogen ratios given COMT AA slow clearance).
⚠ Estriol cream (Dr. West Rx) KEEP — IF TAKING
Weak topical estrogen. ⚠ COMPLIANCE UNCONFIRMED — not in patient self-report.

ASSESSMENT SUMMARY

ASSESSMENT TOTALS
CRITICAL: 3 items (Armour Thyroid status, Estrace compliance, Cyanocobalamin wrong form) MODIFY: 6 items (Vitamin D, Magnesium, LL-37, Progesterone, Lamotrigine, Metformin) KEEP: 18 items (core protocol — genetically supported) OK: 13 items (supportive, may continue) ADD NEW: 1 item (L-Tryptophan — low serotonin) PAUSE: 1 item (TBC Probiotic — environment not ready) UNCONFIRMED: 2 items (Biest cream, Estriol cream — compliance unknown)
IMMEDIATE ACTIONS REQUIRED:
  1. Confirm Armour Thyroid status → reinstate if not taking
  2. Increase Metformin to full 1000mg BID
  3. Increase Lamotrigine to prescribed 100mg/day
  4. Address Estrace vaginal cream non-compliance
  5. Switch progesterone to cyclic dosing (days 10-24)
  6. Discontinue cyanocobalamin IM (WRONG form for MTHFR compound het)
  7. Increase vitamin D dosing for CYP2R1 GG
  8. Start L-Tryptophan 500mg bedtime (serotonin 48, LOW)

4c. TRUAGE ALGORITHM CAVEAT

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  TRUAGE DATA â€” CROSS-YEAR COMPARABILITY WARNING                             â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  2022 TruAge Report:                                                        â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ TruAge Intrinsic: 53.06 years (+7.4 over chrono age 45.6)             â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ TruAge Extrinsic: 54.26 years (+8.6) [UNVERIFIED â€” not in pipeline]   â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Algorithm version: NOT SPECIFIED (pre-2024 methodology)                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  2025 TruAge Report:                                                        â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Symphony Age: 53.1 years (+4.1 over chrono age 49.0)                   â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ OMICm Age: 42.0 years (-7.0)                                           â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ DunedinPACE: 0.90 (aging at 90% rate)                                   â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Brain Organ Age: 54.2 years (+5.2)                                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Algorithm version: Updated 2024-2025 methodology                        â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  CRITICAL NOTE:                                                              â”‚
â”‚  The 2022 and 2025 TruAge reports use DIFFERENT algorithms, clocks,       â”‚
â”‚  and output metrics. They CANNOT be directly compared to track aging      â”‚
â”‚  trajectory. Specifically:                                                  â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 2022: "Intrinsic" and "Extrinsic" age (Horvath-derived)               â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 2025: "Symphony" (multi-clock integration), "OMICm" (multi-omic),     â”‚
â”‚    organ-specific ages, DunedinPACE (rate of aging)                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  The apparent "improvement" from 53.06 (2022) to 53.1 (2025 Symphony)    â”‚
â”‚  CANNOT be attributed to treatment because the measurement tool changed.  â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  VALID COMPARISON: The DunedinPACE of 0.90 (2025) is a standalone        â”‚
â”‚  metric indicating current RATE of aging is favorable (90% of average).   â”‚
â”‚  This suggests current interventions are slowing aging pace even if       â”‚
â”‚  absolute biological age remains elevated.                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  RECOMMENDATION: Use 2025 TruAge as the new baseline. Retest in 12       â”‚
â”‚  months using the same laboratory and algorithm version for valid         â”‚
â”‚  comparison.                                                                â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚

4d. MODEL UNCERTAINTIES

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  HONEST ASSESSMENT â€” WHAT THE MODEL ASSUMES BUT CANNOT FULLY VERIFY       â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  1. 146-SNP LIMITATION                                                      â”‚
â”‚     The 3x4 Genetics panel covers 146 curated SNPs. Full genome-wide      â”‚
â”‚     analysis covers 600,000+. Pathway burden scores have WIDER            â”‚
â”‚     confidence intervals than analyses based on comprehensive genomic     â”‚
â”‚     data (e.g., Case 1767 had 679,085 SNPs).                              â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚     Specific gaps:                                                          â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ MTR bottleneck (85% burden) is INFERRED from the cascade model,    â”‚
â”‚       not from a directly measured risk allele (MTR rs1805087 AA =        â”‚
â”‚       no_impact on this panel). The bottleneck may be less severe        â”‚
â”‚       than modeled.                                                        â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ NOD2 variants (bacterial sensing) not tested â€” cannot assess       â”‚
â”‚       innate immune recognition defects contributing to dysbiosis.       â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ FMO3 variants (trimethylamine metabolism) not tested â€” potential   â”‚
â”‚       gut-related contributor unknown.                                     â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Comprehensive pharmacogenomic profile limited to panel coverage.   â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  2. NO QUESTIONNAIRE DATA                                                   â”‚
â”‚     Symptom-pathway mapping relies entirely on clinical notes and         â”‚
â”‚     patient self-report (single document, circa Dec 2025). No validated  â”‚
â”‚     questionnaires (PHQ-9, MSQ, PSQI, etc.) were available.              â”‚
â”‚     This means:                                                             â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Symptom severity is estimated from clinical context, not measured  â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Brain fog, fatigue, and histamine symptom burden are qualitative   â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Treatment response tracking has no quantified baseline             â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  3. THYROID MEDICATION STATUS IS UNKNOWN                                    â”‚
â”‚     This fundamentally changes the interpretation of:                      â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ TSH 1.24 (treated euthyroid vs natural euthyroid)                  â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ IR Score trajectory (thyroid contribution unknown)                   â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Brain fog causation (brain T3 deficit magnitude unknown)            â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Gut motility (thyroid-driven component magnitude unknown)           â”‚
â”‚     Until this is resolved, Protocol #1 recommendations are              â”‚
â”‚     provisional and may require revision.                                  â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  4. BIOMARKER COMPARABILITY ACROSS TIME                                     â”‚
â”‚     Labs were drawn across 15+ collection dates (2018-2025) from         â”‚
â”‚     multiple laboratories (Quest, Vibrant, Genova, Cleveland HeartLab,   â”‚
â”‚     True Health Diagnostics, Vitae). Reference ranges and assay          â”‚
â”‚     methods differ. Trends identified in Part 1 assume comparability     â”‚
â”‚     across labs and time periods. Some apparent trends (particularly      â”‚
â”‚     in markers like LDL-P, ferritin, thyroid) may partially reflect     â”‚
â”‚     methodological differences rather than true clinical change.          â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  5. SUPPLEMENT FORMULATION UNKNOWN                                          â”‚
â”‚     Several supplements (Inflamafree, Cholesterol Complete, Brilliant     â”‚
â”‚     Brain, TBC Probiotic, Cyclease Menopause, Vitamin D Sun 30,         â”‚
â”‚     Ultimate Recovery, Gabatrol) are proprietary blends. Exact            â”‚
â”‚     ingredient lists and doses were not available in patient records.     â”‚
â”‚     KEEP/OK assessments for these are based on general product           â”‚
â”‚     category, not confirmed formulation.                                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  6. CAUSAL MODEL LIMITATIONS                                                â”‚
â”‚     The endotype model ("The Slow Burn") is a HYPOTHESIS that best       â”‚
â”‚     fits the available data. Alternative causal models exist. The        â”‚
â”‚     convergence of multiple genetic variants is probabilistic, not       â”‚
â”‚     deterministic. Individual response to interventions may differ       â”‚
â”‚     from model predictions. The 4-pass endotyping pipeline produces     â”‚
â”‚     pathway burden scores that are estimates, not measurements.          â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â”‚  7. EPIGENETIC AGE RELIABILITY                                              â”‚
â”‚     Organ-specific epigenetic ages (brain 54.2, blood 54.5, immune      â”‚
â”‚     53.6) are emerging metrics with moderate clinical validation.        â”‚
â”‚     They should be treated as HYPOTHESIS-GENERATING data, not as        â”‚
â”‚     diagnostic certainties. The DunedinPACE (0.90) is better validated  â”‚
â”‚     but still a population-level metric applied to an individual.        â”‚
â”‚                                                                              â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
